members of our team said if she was involved they were not continuing with WFAF. Our goal

and the 12/12 event that it wasn't realistic time wise to replace her.

us at the time) ... This is right after Alex attacked/threatened me and the police were involved 
on 12/11. When Cindy realized that she was no longer going to be a part of WFAF or the 
bus tour, she went and removed WFAF from the NPS permit for 1/6. When we learned of

removed from the permit and it was placed back in WFAF's name.

Hi Ms. Kremer. Curt Devine with the news network CNN here. I'm writing because my 
colleagues and I are working on a two-hour documentary about individuals who came to 
Washington DC on January 6th. A goal of this documentary is not to focus on the events of 
that day at the Capitol (which have been heavily covered), but rather to understand more 
about the perspectives of people who were there and to more fully explore the political 
context and values surrounding that day and the election at large. 
In all seriousness, we would value including your perspective in this. I'm not sure if you would 
even entertain the idea of this, but we would be very interested in hearing your take. Given 
the length of this project, this would not be about simply getting one sound bite from you, 
but would be a long-form interview that could be a through-line of much of the documentary. 
We would want to hear from your reflections on all of this and what you think people (like 
typical CNN viewers) may not understand. 
If you're open to considering this, please give me a call or feel free to write back here. I'd be 
happy to speak more off record about this. Thanks either way, 
Curt Devine

Amy Kremer-6/8/2021 7:48 PM 
6/8/202 1 7:48 PM . . . 
Former President Donald Trump's post-election political team has fired one of its top 
fundraisers who played a key role in organizing the January 6 "Save America Rally" that 
preceded Trump supporters· attack on the US Capitol, Republican strategists and Trump 
advisors told Insider. 
The Trump-approved group America Alliance fired veteran fundraiser Caroline Wren at the end 
of last month, according to the Trump advisors. Other Trump fundraising groups sent cease­
and-desist letters to Wren demanding she not cite Trump in her own efforts to recruit high­
dollar donors, they said. 
A Republican familiar with the break-up said Wren left America Alliance but wasn't fired, 
and that Trump associates did not send her cease-and-desist letters from any of the myriad 
political groups claiming the Trump mantle. 
Trump advisors told Insider that Wren tried to control Republicans donors and fought with 
other pro-Trump operatives. 
Wren's forceful entrance on the Trump fundraising circuit at a series of events in late April 
particularly spooked Trump's advisors, the strategist said. 
"She was moving in on their turf, so I'm not surprised to see they're gunning at her now," a 
Republican strategist said. 
"Caroline was terminated last month," said one Trump advisor familiar with her departure . "She 
was causing a lot of chaos and not raising money" in the months after Trump lost the 2020 
presidential election. 
But other Republicans said Wren got caught in the turbulence of Trump's ever-changing, post­
election political efforts as she attempted to extract herself from Trump's political team and 
start her own, yet-to-be-named network of conservative donors to bankroll Republican races 
up and down the ballot. 
"She's just a fundraiser that emerged out of nowhere after the election and was in the middle 
of everything ," the Republican strategist of the spat between Wren and Trumpworld .
